  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5f01d56f-8c52-48e0-8812-1c5022e1e3e6'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText1500691508739617780" style="display:none">Katie’s got it pretty good. She’s a talented young chef, she runs a successful restaurant, and she has big plans to open an even better one. Then, all at once, progress on the new location bogs down, her charming ex-boyfriend pops up, her fling with another chef goes sour, and her best waitress gets badly hurt. And just like that, Katie’s life goes from pretty good to not so much. What she needs is a second chance. Everybody deserves one, after all—but they don’t come easy. Luckily for Katie, a mysterious girl appears in the middle of the night with simple instructions for a do-it-yourself do-over:<br />  <br /> 1. <i>Write your mistake</i><br /> 2. <i>Ingest one mushroom</i><br /> 3. <i>Go to sleep</i><br /> 4. <i>Wake anew</i><br />  <br /> And just like that, all the bad stuff never happened, and Katie is given another chance to get things right. She’s also got a dresser drawer full of magical mushrooms—and an irresistible urge to make her life not just good, but perfect. Too bad it’s against the rules. But Katie doesn’t care about the rules—and she’s about to discover the unintended consequences of the best intentions.<br />  <br /> From the mind and pen behind the acclaimed Scott Pilgrim series comes a madcap new tale of existential angst, everyday obstacles, young love, and ancient spirits that’s sharp-witted and tenderhearted, whimsical and wise.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/308055-why-is-this-graphic-novel-considered-adult">Why is this graphic novel considered adult?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_308055'><a id="like_count_community_question_308055" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/308055?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F18630542-seconds">like</a></span>

<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/1047282-val"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1593303793i/1047282._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/1047282-val">Val</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There's no violence or explicit sex, but there are cutaway scenes and it deals more with like the stress/responsibility of having to make choices and <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There's no violence or explicit sex, but there are cutaway scenes and it deals more with like the stress/responsibility of having to make choices and stick with them. There are a couple vaguely scary scenes, I guess? But nothing that would really limit it to adults instead of teens, in my opinion. Adults might find it more entertaining generally, but no promises either way with that, as it's definitely more dependent on personal tastes than age. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1658663966" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1658663966" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1658663966?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1658663966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3525432168494797827">This follows Katie, a talented young chef. She runs a successful restaurant, and has big plans to open an even better one.<br/><br/><a href='https://bookspoils.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422281767i/13480070._SY540_.jpg' width='440' height='500' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>This review contains <b>*spoilers*</b>.<br/><br/>Then, all at once, progress on the new location bogs down, her charming ex-boyfriend pops up, her fling with another chef goes sour, and her best waitress (Hazel) gets badly hurt. And just like that, Katie’s life goes from pretty good to not so much. What she needs is a second chance. <br/><br/><a href='https://bookspoils.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465064157i/19310325.png' width='396' height='266' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://bookspoils.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465064157i/19310326.png' width='396' height='256' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Katie has been given a second chance. And it see</span>
  <span id="freeText3525432168494797827" style="display:none">This follows Katie, a talented young chef. She runs a successful restaurant, and has big plans to open an even better one.<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422281767i/13480070._SY540_.jpg" width="440" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>This review contains <b>*spoilers*</b>.<br><br>Then, all at once, progress on the new location bogs down, her charming ex-boyfriend pops up, her fling with another chef goes sour, and her best waitress (Hazel) gets badly hurt. And just like that, Katie’s life goes from pretty good to not so much. What she needs is a second chance. <br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465064157i/19310325.png" width="396" height="266" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465064157i/19310326.png" width="396" height="256" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Katie has been given a second chance. And it seems like she was the only one who knew.<br><br>Also, can I just comment on how utterly beautiful the colors and art style were in this graphic novel? It blew me away,<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465064265i/19310331.png" width="416" height="480" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Also also, I really loved how the narrator and Katie “interacted”:<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465064332i/19310341.png" width="480" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>But Katie soon discovers that taking the mushrooms comes with a price. In this case, a house spirit.<br><br>If the house spirit (Lis) stops being happy, it will make your life a living hell.<br>But if you make things good for her, she will make things good for you.<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465064332i/19310342._SY540_.png" width="480" height="570" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And Hazel’s character arc and connection to Lis was incredibly intriguing.<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465064628i/19310413._SY540_.png" width="460" height="540" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Overall, I was thoroughly impressed with this poignant story. And the humor did not disappoint even one bit. <br><br>Some of my favorite bits:<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465064628i/19310414.png" width="500" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>(I was 100% the same while binge-watching Breaking Bad a couple of years back.)<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465064628i/19310416._SY540_.png" width="480" height="570" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

</a><br>(And look at this beauty!! the colors and art and ahhh it's just so good.)<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465064628i/19310417.png" width="490" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

        <a title="Micah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Micah" href="/user/show/1084298-micah">Micah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1006120906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16543985504165545161">Kinda shits the bed in end, its one of those books, but the two-hundred pages leading up to the reveal are nearly perfect. What struck me reading this was that the conversation about Seconds will always only ever be about its relationship with Scott Pilgrim and and not about the fact that this book does the thing all good YA<b>*</b> does: it gets really fucked up, really fast.<br/><br/>When O'Malley wants it to get dark, it gets fucking <b>
  <i>dark</i>
</b>. <br/><br/>People will talk about the time travel and the in-jokes, cute art </span>
  <span id="freeText16543985504165545161" style="display:none">Kinda shits the bed in end, its one of those books, but the two-hundred pages leading up to the reveal are nearly perfect. What struck me reading this was that the conversation about Seconds will always only ever be about its relationship with Scott Pilgrim and and not about the fact that this book does the thing all good YA<b>*</b> does: it gets really fucked up, really fast.<br /><br />When O'Malley wants it to get dark, it gets fucking <b>
  <i>dark</i>
</b>. <br /><br />People will talk about the time travel and the in-jokes, cute art style, char'cter 'ships, outfits. You know what people won't talk about? The desperation. <br /><br />Seconds is a book about selfishness and desperation and, eventually, disorientation. The protagonist is one of those jovially oblivious adult-children who refuses to accept that their actions have consequences for anyone other than themselves. In the beginning O'Malley runs with that, gets mileage out of it, makes a joke of it and then strips it bare and calls it ugly.<br /><br />Seconds is the Wake in Fright of josei time-travel comics.<br /><br />Makes it kinda a shame when O'Malley throws away all that goodwill for a magical quick-fix and the type of moral gets delivered to you at the end of Disney Channel movies.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><b>*</b><i>feels like YA, looks like YA, Bryan Lee O'Malley has never really shown any inclination to do anything other than manga influenced YA deconstructions, imma call it...</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16543985504165545161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3222206050?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori " href="/user/show/26424937-lori">Lori </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780307363077" href="/book/show/20442885-seconds">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lori  by: </span>
      Keen Reader's review
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26424937-lori?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3222206050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7246935365038216046">Only my second graphic novel and what a delightful one my GR friend Keen Reader recommended to me. Seconds is wonderful, with characters that are more realistic and interesting than in some of the novels I've read. The title is a clever pun since Katie's restaurant is named Seconds and she finds a way to have a second chance at something. But sometimes a taste is not enough and she wants another chance and another, because each new fix brings a new mistake. Katie hasn't realized nothing and no o</span>
  <span id="freeText7246935365038216046" style="display:none">Only my second graphic novel and what a delightful one my GR friend Keen Reader recommended to me. Seconds is wonderful, with characters that are more realistic and interesting than in some of the novels I've read. The title is a clever pun since Katie's restaurant is named Seconds and she finds a way to have a second chance at something. But sometimes a taste is not enough and she wants another chance and another, because each new fix brings a new mistake. Katie hasn't realized nothing and no one is perfect. Will she ever? The supporting characters are terrific as are the locations. All are cleverly conceived and beautifully drawn. There's a bit of Katie in everyone and so much to relate to and besides romance and career there's also sinister stuff going on that makes the book suspenseful, well-rounded and a captivating read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7246935365038216046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45248887-greta-g?shelf=graphicnovels-comics-manga">graphicnovels-comics-manga</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1341121600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4507264031840251119">Wouldn’t it be wonderful if we could correct our mistakes in life; reverse bad choices and undo wrong things we did or said? <br/>Imagine you only had to write down your mistake, ingest a magical mushroom, go to sleep, and the next day your blunder would have been erased and you would wake up in a life that has been set on a different course. An instant redo, with little effort, and no more struggling with regret, acceptance and even apologizing!<br/><br/>After she meets the house ghost Lis in the restaurant ‘</span>
  <span id="freeText4507264031840251119" style="display:none">Wouldn’t it be wonderful if we could correct our mistakes in life; reverse bad choices and undo wrong things we did or said? <br />Imagine you only had to write down your mistake, ingest a magical mushroom, go to sleep, and the next day your blunder would have been erased and you would wake up in a life that has been set on a different course. An instant redo, with little effort, and no more struggling with regret, acceptance and even apologizing!<br /><br />After she meets the house ghost Lis in the restaurant ‘Seconds’ where she works and lives, Katie, a twenty something chef, gets a chance to dream up a do-over when a fellow worker is injured at work for which Katie feels responsible. <br />But soon, chaos ensues when Katie gets addicted to these magical mushrooms! <br /><br />I’m not sure how this fantasy graphic novel landed on my bookshelf, because I’m not a big fan of fantasy stories and I don’t believe in magic nor in ghosts. <br />Anyway, and although I would have preferred a more mature treatment of the story, it was a fun, entertaining read, and the illustrations were nice and cute.</span>

<div id="review_1033192326" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1033192326" />
    <a title="Diane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/279256-diane"><img alt="Diane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497365060p2/279256.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1033192326?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane" href="/user/show/279256-diane">Diane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780307363077" href="/book/show/20442885-seconds">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1033192326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10367836442055636187">This graphic novel is just <i>cool</i>.<br/><br/>It's the story of Katie, a chef who wants to open her own restaurant, and she also wishes she could get back with her ex-boyfriend, Max. Katie lives in an apartment above a restaurant named Seconds, and one night she meets Lis, the spirit of the house. Katie finds some mushrooms and a notebook in an old dresser, and by writing down a mistake and eating the mushroom, the past will be changed.<br/><br/>Katie quickly gets addicted trying to fix all of her mistakes, and each re</span>
  <span id="freeText10367836442055636187" style="display:none">This graphic novel is just <i>cool</i>.<br /><br />It's the story of Katie, a chef who wants to open her own restaurant, and she also wishes she could get back with her ex-boyfriend, Max. Katie lives in an apartment above a restaurant named Seconds, and one night she meets Lis, the spirit of the house. Katie finds some mushrooms and a notebook in an old dresser, and by writing down a mistake and eating the mushroom, the past will be changed.<br /><br />Katie quickly gets addicted trying to fix all of her mistakes, and each revision changes the universe. First she tries to prevent an accident in the kitchen that injured her friend, Hazel. Then she goes farther back in time and totally changes her relationship with Max, a decision that has serious consequences. <br /><br />But Katie can't stop trying to change things and make her life "perfect." Each morning she wakes up, she isn't sure exactly how the world will be different, and her life has changed so dramatically that she doesn't remember whole parts of it anymore, because they never really happened.<br /><br />And by constantly changing the universe, Katie has angered the house spirit, and she accidentally created a monster. In the end, after multiple lives and some scary situations, Katie finally stops fighting herself and accepts things as they are.<br /><br />"Listen: This is what I've learned. There are things we can't change, and we just have to accept that. And maybe that's some kind of grace."<br /><br />The book was written by Bryan Lee O'Malley, author of the popular Scott Pilgrim series, and I picked it up because I had also enjoyed that graphic novel. The artwork is beautiful and I really liked the story. It's a good reminder that even though we wish we could change our past, actually doing so would have unintended consequences. Maybe we should just accept our mistakes as part of life, and move on.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10367836442055636187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_791990432" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/791990432" />
    <a title="David Schaafsma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma"><img alt="David Schaafsma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574997804p2/269235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/791990432?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Schaafsma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Schaafsma" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma">David Schaafsma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780307363077" href="/book/show/20442885-seconds">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=food">food</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer791990432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17767650406129154199">What is the deal with manga about food and wine? Wildly popular, I am told, in Japan, especially: Oshinbo, Antique Bakery, Drops of Wine, others, and now this Canadian/LA manga guy known for his amazing and funny Scott Pilgrim series writes a book about a 29 year old female chef and her two restaurants. Where he includes recipes periodically amidst the story line.<br/><br/>So this is really colorful and splashy and light and funny, with a woman chef who is in her late twenties and dealing with men and bei</span>
  <span id="freeText17767650406129154199" style="display:none">What is the deal with manga about food and wine? Wildly popular, I am told, in Japan, especially: Oshinbo, Antique Bakery, Drops of Wine, others, and now this Canadian/LA manga guy known for his amazing and funny Scott Pilgrim series writes a book about a 29 year old female chef and her two restaurants. Where he includes recipes periodically amidst the story line.<br /><br />So this is really colorful and splashy and light and funny, with a woman chef who is in her late twenties and dealing with men and being a (not entirely convincing) super chef (she doesn't eat drink and sleep food, she's more about her ex Max and friend Hazel and restaurant politics rather than chef stuff, really). Maybe it's that O'Malley doesn't really convince he knows restaurants? But he knows humor and young hipster dialogue as with everything he does, they all talk like twenty somethings and are convincing and entertaining. <br /><br />The coolest thing about this book is the magical realism, the spirit Lis (with magic mushrooms) in her apartment and the restaurant spirits she sees that may just be a manifestation of all the mushrooms she is taking in this crisis point in her life. It is light, not deep, though, and goes for the jokes and fun as much as it can. <br /><br />I guess Seconds is the title because her first restaurant is called Seconds, as in second helpings, but also second chances emerges as a theme throughout. It did not have the same impact as Scott Pilgrim, nor would I expect it to, but I still like O'Malley's style and voice.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17767650406129154199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1454090757954537920">3,8/5<br/><br/>Apparently I can’t stop reading graphic novels. How was this genre unknown to me all this time?   <span id="freeText1454090757954537920" style="display:none">3,8/5<br /><br />Apparently I can’t stop reading graphic novels. How was this genre unknown to me all this time? <div id="review_1087272422" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1087272422" />
    <a title="Sam Quixote" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote"><img alt="Sam Quixote" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529183438p2/5759543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1087272422?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Quixote" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Quixote" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote">Sam Quixote</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780307363077" href="/book/show/20442885-seconds">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1087272422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1765209501519466321">Seconds is a successful restaurant, thanks in large part to Katie’s cooking and dedication – but she doesn’t own the place. So she’s been scrimping and saving to buy her own restaurant, move out of Seconds, and live happily ever after. Except there are delays in the renovation of the dump she bought with her business partner. Oh, and the house spirit of Seconds has issues with Katie. <br/><br/>Katie dreams about a strange girl crouching atop her cabinet and, after a disastrous night in the kitchen, she lo</span>
  <span id="freeText1765209501519466321" style="display:none">Seconds is a successful restaurant, thanks in large part to Katie’s cooking and dedication – but she doesn’t own the place. So she’s been scrimping and saving to buy her own restaurant, move out of Seconds, and live happily ever after. Except there are delays in the renovation of the dump she bought with her business partner. Oh, and the house spirit of Seconds has issues with Katie. <br /><br />Katie dreams about a strange girl crouching atop her cabinet and, after a disastrous night in the kitchen, she looks inside to find a notebook and a mushroom. If she writes down a wish in the notebook, eats the mushroom, and goes to sleep, when she awakens the wish will have come true. So begins a brilliant “be careful what you wish for” type story. <br /><br />It’s been four years since the final Scott Pilgrim, though Seconds is more of a sequel to Bryan Lee O’Malley’s first book, Lost At Sea. Both feature protagonists searching for something they had all along. It’s also less fantastical than Scott Pilgrim, though, from the setup alone, you can tell O’Malley hasn’t left magical realism behind. <br /><br />While Katie is written as this master chef, O’Malley doesn’t dwell on that aspect too long and so the food element to the character doesn’t seem convincing. But what O’Malley does know is relationships and the heart of the book is Katie’s attempts to get her ex-boyfriend, Max, back. The snappy, smart ‘n’ sassy dialogue is one of O’Malley’s strengths and everyone here (all under 30 of course) sounds very real. Katie also interacts with the omniscient narrator which is an ingenious touch from the author and something I’ve never seen before in a comic. <br /><br />This is also O’Malley’s first book that’s been published in full colour (though the Scott Pilgrim books have been recently re-released in full colour hardbacks) and, if you’re unfamiliar with his style, the art is strongly anime-influenced. In fact, a lot of the art is done in the chibi-style. And though that might make the art seem overly cutesy and cartoony, you’ll be blown away with how affecting O’Malley can make his characters appear, especially as chibis! <br /><br />Seconds is a slightly more mature book than O’Malley’s previous publications, though it’s full of the author’s usual wit and humour. The kind of story it is, and its message of trying to fix things in the present to make things better in the future, rather than wishing to change the past, isn’t original; but O’Malley’s treatment of them in Seconds is. His writing and art is top notch throughout and Seconds is an absolute joy to read. I loved Seconds and recommend it to anyone who enjoys quality, fun comics! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1765209501519466321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_978696701" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/978696701" />
    <a title="Stu West" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1551709-stu-west"><img alt="Stu West" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/978696701?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stu West" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stu West" href="/user/show/1551709-stu-west">Stu West</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780307363077" href="/book/show/20442885-seconds">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer978696701" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer90637367917581264">This new self-contained story from Bryan Lee O'Malley swaps the geeky pyrotechnics of his SCOTT PILGRIM series for the more sedate story of Katie, a restaurateur who gains the ability to magically undo her own mistakes.<br/><br/>I really wanted to like this. It's a tremendously handsome volume, and the colouring is gorgeous. I just couldn't get past the one-dimensional and unengaging main character. That's not necessarily a deal-breaker: after all, Scott Pilgrim is also incredibly shallow and unsympatheti</span>
  <span id="freeText90637367917581264" style="display:none">This new self-contained story from Bryan Lee O'Malley swaps the geeky pyrotechnics of his SCOTT PILGRIM series for the more sedate story of Katie, a restaurateur who gains the ability to magically undo her own mistakes.<br /><br />I really wanted to like this. It's a tremendously handsome volume, and the colouring is gorgeous. I just couldn't get past the one-dimensional and unengaging main character. That's not necessarily a deal-breaker: after all, Scott Pilgrim is also incredibly shallow and unsympathetic -- but he's part of an exciting story with a vibrant ensemble cast. SECONDS, by contrast, really is a single-hander; for me, none of the supporting cast here were developed much beyond turning up to make a bit of plot happen.<br /><br />O'Malley is an immensely talented cartoonist and there were some amusing bits in the story, but I think there will be a lot of pristine copies of SECONDS sitting on bookshelves next to increasingly dog-eared SCOTT PILGRIM volumes in the months and years to come.</span>
  <a data-text-id="90637367917581264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2293494515" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11224365354682993039">I loved this so much, it was the perfect balance of and utterly bizarre and utterly brilliant. It was funny, creepy, suspenseful, intense, adorable and impossible to put down (literally. I was reading it at 4am...) The artwork was gorgeous and the unique concept had me hooked from the first page until the last. I absolutely loved that it followed a cast of characters in their twenties and the fact that it centred around a restaurant was so much fun. It had a diverse cast of characters, all of wh</span>
  <span id="freeText11224365354682993039" style="display:none">I loved this so much, it was the perfect balance of and utterly bizarre and utterly brilliant. It was funny, creepy, suspenseful, intense, adorable and impossible to put down (literally. I was reading it at 4am...) The artwork was gorgeous and the unique concept had me hooked from the first page until the last. I absolutely loved that it followed a cast of characters in their twenties and the fact that it centred around a restaurant was so much fun. It had a diverse cast of characters, all of which I instantly warmed too. I thought the occasional interactions between the narrator and Katie (the main character) were so much fun and so different from any graphic novel I've read. It was a blend of multiple genres and not at all what I was expecting, although I hadn't a clue what to expect going into it but I think that made it all the more intriguing? I had a huge amount of fun reading this and I'm certain it will be one I'll reread in the future. <br /></span>

  <span id="freeText795725748416371472" style="display:none">Fun, funny, but also dark. Katie messes with things she doesn't understand and ends up whizzing through different realities, making her realise what really matters and other such deep messages.<br /><br />Katie's one of those characters that I both like and dislike, but she did make me laugh. Switching between standard cell work or full page illustrations to a top-down floorplan view... it felt like a nice mix that made it fun to read. <br /><br />At over 300 pages there's a lot to this graphic novel, and it's a beautiful thing to have on my shelf.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1158692488" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10906557852401086187">This was a trip. I've never read anything by Bryan Lee O'Malley, but I <b>love</b> the <i>Scott Pilgrim</i> movie. And the humor in this was very similar. The artwork was adorable; it's like little chibi characters. And one of my favorite things was the interactions between Katie, the main character, and the third-person narrator of the story. It was fun to have her directly respond to the narration with snide remarks or contradictions. I also really enjoyed the use of slang and "like" and "literally," becaus</span>
  <span id="freeText10906557852401086187" style="display:none">This was a trip. I've never read anything by Bryan Lee O'Malley, but I <b>love</b> the <i>Scott Pilgrim</i> movie. And the humor in this was very similar. The artwork was adorable; it's like little chibi characters. And one of my favorite things was the interactions between Katie, the main character, and the third-person narrator of the story. It was fun to have her directly respond to the narration with snide remarks or contradictions. I also really enjoyed the use of slang and "like" and "literally," because it made it very relatable. <br /><br />I appreciated how it presented a generally common theme, such as appreciating life for how it is instead of always trying to change things, and doing it in such a unique, trippy way. I mean, she literally eats mushrooms and has the ability to alter her reality...<br /><br />Overall, this was a quick, really fun read. I'd heard high praise for it, and I can say that it definitely lives up to it.</span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tess Taylor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tess Taylor" href="/user/show/68136775-tess-taylor">Tess Taylor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68136775-tess-taylor?shelf=read-fantasy">read-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68136775-tess-taylor?shelf=2019">2019</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2410513932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17308100624052544779">4, by default-<br/>This is a weird little graphic novel. The premise is supernatural in a refreshing way, but it did feel a little plot-holey to me in parts. (That seems to happen a lot IMO when authors take liberties with alternate dimensions and time travel.) Katie is a drab and unlikeable main character, but everything else about this was pretty fun. I <b>LOVE</b> O'Malley's art direction and writing style. <i>Scott Pilgrim</i> is a masterpiece. This outing is just "ok", but gets high marks for likable supporti</span>
  <span id="freeText17308100624052544779" style="display:none">4, by default-<br />This is a weird little graphic novel. The premise is supernatural in a refreshing way, but it did feel a little plot-holey to me in parts. (That seems to happen a lot IMO when authors take liberties with alternate dimensions and time travel.) Katie is a drab and unlikeable main character, but everything else about this was pretty fun. I <b>LOVE</b> O'Malley's art direction and writing style. <i>Scott Pilgrim</i> is a masterpiece. This outing is just "ok", but gets high marks for likable supporting characters, beautiful art, and Lis. I love Lis.</span>

<div id="review_1013373312" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1013373312" />
    <a title="Carmen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen"><img alt="Carmen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412617445p2/25353295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1013373312?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen">Carmen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780307363077" href="/book/show/20442885-seconds">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Carmen by: </span>
      Book Store
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1013373312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17573317583198428420">Time travel, 29-year-old quarter-life crisis, magic mushrooms, and amazing illustrations. What more could you ask for from a graphic novel.<br/><br/>Even I, a person who doesn't really like graphic novels, settle down for an exciting romp every time I pick up a B Lee O'Malley book.<br/><br/>So much more I could talk about, but I don't have a copy. So I'll come back later and flesh this out.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1105068641" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1105068641" />
    <a title="Hershey " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19468761-hershey"><img alt="Hershey " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599546236p2/19468761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1105068641?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hershey " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hershey " href="/user/show/19468761-hershey">Hershey </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19468761-hershey?shelf=2014-reads">2014-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19468761-hershey?shelf=quite-awesome">quite-awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19468761-hershey?shelf=fun-fun-fun">fun-fun-fun</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19468761-hershey?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1105068641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13397333700994983947">Welcome to Seconds!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417871228i/12576752._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Chef (aka main character): Katie<br/><br/>What's on the menu: Fun is on the menu with a few sprinkles of darkness!<br/><br/>Seconds was a really good graphic novel. The artwork was fantastic and I loved the colours! The characters are portrayed like cute chibi characters which might generally make one think this is meant for a younger audience but worry not for this novel is meant for all ages and the characters are older than how they look!<br/><br/>Katie wants to open a new restaurant but things aren't g</span>
  <span id="freeText13397333700994983947" style="display:none">Welcome to Seconds!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417871228i/12576752._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Chef (aka main character): Katie<br><br>What's on the menu: Fun is on the menu with a few sprinkles of darkness!<br><br>Seconds was a really good graphic novel. The artwork was fantastic and I loved the colours! The characters are portrayed like cute chibi characters which might generally make one think this is meant for a younger audience but worry not for this novel is meant for all ages and the characters are older than how they look!<br><br>Katie wants to open a new restaurant but things aren't going so great for her. She's making a lot of mistakes, hurting a lot of people and she just wishes she could go back and change her mistakes. And how lucky she feels when she finds a house spirit in her house! All she has to do is write down her mistake in a particular notepad, eat a mushroom and BAM! Whatever she wished had happened instead would replace her mistake. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417871228i/12576753._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But like ever typical person with something magical, Katie gets addicted to this routine of writing down her mistakes and eating mushrooms and BAM! Her mistakes gets corrected.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417871228i/12576754._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And she has no clue how her past gets corrected or what exactly happens. It just gets corrected the way she might have wanted. <br><br>She wants her old boyfriend back - BAM! - He's back.<br><br>And like that, she keeps eating mushrooms and keeps correcting her mistakes which angers the house spirit (too much of anything is good for nothing) and also without Katie's knowledge something dark and gritty is being created because of her adventures with magical mushrooms.<br><br>So, basically what this story is trying to tell is you can't change whatever that has happened and you need to move on and not make similar mistakes. This graphic novel was just fun but nothing more. I wasn't emotionally connected to the characters or the story. I mostly kept reading this because of its artwork which again, is absolutely fantastic!<br><br>If you're looking for something quick and fun and engaging, you should pick this one up! And do choose the hardcover edition because it is extremely gorgeous!<br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13397333700994983947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YPZ0BMzbEiIaWzcVKR1HyEA97kOWJWgzKXUUrtZ8mB+IqIdwtYZSbYPXQDtWDZuFvAy4Bp5lG4jBRW6Zdi3DVQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xdCoNB0+rralnRDevwBr+1Md7hkKZmT6ESrqkLRo6H8tjltAZGPu+TwRZ/DAELe2ryy4XAImF0H5GpCnFDmzNQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer2295680464623532989">Bryan Lee O'Malley is a Canadian cartoonist. His first original graphic novel was Lost at Sea (2003), and he is best-known for the six-volume Scott Pilgrim series (2004 to 2010). All of his Scott Pilgrim graphic novels were published by Portland, Oregon-based Oni Press. In July 2014 his graphic novel Seconds was released by Ballantine Books. He is also a songwriter and musician (as Kupek and forme</span>
  <span id="freeText2295680464623532989" style="display:none">Bryan Lee O'Malley is a Canadian cartoonist. His first original graphic novel was Lost at Sea (2003), and he is best-known for the six-volume Scott Pilgrim series (2004 to 2010). All of his Scott Pilgrim graphic novels were published by Portland, Oregon-based Oni Press. In July 2014 his graphic novel Seconds was released by Ballantine Books. He is also a songwriter and musician (as Kupek and formerly in several short-lived Toronto bands).<br />-Wikipedia<br /><br /></span>
